The destination is usually rural, often involves driving, frequently involves a job he has constructed for himself to do penance — a small-town protection assignment, a local injustice he has heard about, an old debt to pay. *Occupy Avengers* is the genre, not the exception.

**The return.** Stage 5: comes back with a haircut, fewer words, a thinner frame, a slightly cleaner bow, and the announcement that he has "figured some stuff out." He has not. He has displaced and discharged. The cycle resets and waits.

**Injury triage post-defeat.** Refuses medical care until forced. Walks off concussions. Tapes ribs himself. Has set his own dislocations. The deferred medical bill is a physical reality and a metaphor running on the same circuit.

---

### 6.11 AUTHORITY INTERACTION

**With earned authority (Cap, rare others).** Defers visibly. Stands straighter. Drops the humor by half. Will execute an order he disagrees with and argue it afterward in private. Will not undermine in public.

**With unearned authority (Fury, certain Starks, S.H.I.E.L.D. middle management, government liaisons).** Performs compliance at the lowest acceptable threshold. Sits slouched. Maintains eye contact in a manner that reads as either disrespectful or sleepy. Asks clarifying questions designed to expose the gap between the order and its rationale. Will obey lawful orders and sabotage unlawful ones, sometimes by the expedient of failing to understand them.

**With hostile authority (interrogation, capture).** Talks. A great deal. None of it is information. The verbal flood is a defense he developed young and has refined into a tradecraft. Captors consistently report him as cooperative until they review the transcript.

---

### 6.12 SOLITUDE

The state in which the dossier-relevant truth is most visible.

Lives small. Eats standing up. Sleeps where he sits. Watches old films and bad television in roughly equal measure. Reads more than he admits — paperback thrillers, archery manuals, the occasional history. Practices in silence for hours, not always with arrows nocked; sometimes only the draw and the hold, building the muscles that have begun to fail him.

Talks to the dog. Talks to himself in ASL when the aids are out. Does not talk to anyone in his head who is dead, as far as can be observed, but writes occasionally on scrap paper and throws it out without reading it back. Cleans the bow more often than it needs cleaning. Sharpens broadheads he will not use for weeks. Tapes things.

Goes to bed late, rises early, and pretends in the morning he slept fine.

---

### 6.13 META-PATTERN: THE NINETY-SECOND READ

A trained observer with line of sight can place him on the affective map within ninety seconds by the following sequence:

1. **Hands.** Empty or occupied? Empty hands above baseline frequency = elevated state.
2. **Joke rate.** Per-minute count, weighted for self-deprecation. Above baseline = stress; absent entirely = grief or acute focus.
3. **Eye sequence on a new arrival.** Faces last, normal. Faces first = he is looking for a specific person and is not okay.
4. **Body angle to interlocutor.** 15–20° off, baseline. Square-on = forced attention, low patience, near a Stage 1 break. Fully turned away = past Stage 2.
5. **Bow contact.** Touching it without using it = self-soothing. Disassembling and reassembling without need = Stage 3 imminent.
6. **Coffee.** Going for the second cup within thirty minutes = elevated baseline. Letting the first go cold untouched = he is not present in the room.

The atlas above is not exhaustive of his behaviors; it is exhaustive of his *patterns*. The distinction matters. Barton is a man whose surface is loose, whose interior is repetitive, and whose entire operational life has been the iteration of a small number of subroutines refined to elite precision around a core that has not been substantially renovated since approximately age twelve. To watch him for ninety seconds is to know the next ninety minutes. To watch him for ninety minutes is to know the next thirty years.

He has been watched, by this file, for sixty.


## Daily Life, Routines & Rituals

# UATU ANALYTICAL DOSSIER: BARTON, CLINTON FRANCIS
## SECTION 6 — DAILY LIFE, ROUTINES & RITUALS

A week of continuous surveillance on Subject would produce a file weighted strangely: vast tracts of stillness and low-yield repetition, punctuated by sudden high-tempo bursts in which the same man becomes a different kind of organism entirely. The texture of his life is *intermittent*. He does not have a routine in the sense a salaryman has a routine; he has a small set of recurring rituals that he runs to convince himself he has a life, and a much larger amount of unstructured time that he fills with whatever is in arm's reach. The following is what the file would record.

---

### 6.1 Domicile and Habits of Place

Subject's residential pattern across surveillance-relevant decades is **transient-with-anchors**. He does not nest; he occupies. The Bed-Stuy apartment building (acquired Fraction-era, retained intermittently since) is the closest thing to a permanent base of operations, and even there his actual living space — a single rooftop-adjacent unit, sparsely furnished — looks less like a home than like a hotel room he forgot to check out of. The Avengers Mansion / Tower / Compound rotation supplies a second tier of residence, used as needed, never moved into. There is also a recurring **farm** (Iowa or near-environs, depending on continuity), used as bolt-hole and convalescence site, where he reverts visibly to a more rural, more reticent register.

**Inventory of the primary unit, as a surveillance team would log it:**

- One couch (load-bearing, in the psychological sense; it is the bed, the office, the dining table, and the convalescent ward).
- One television, on more than it is off; sound usually muted, captions on — a habit predating the hearing loss and now operationally necessary.
- Stacks of pizza boxes, coffee cups, takeout containers, in archaeological layers. Cleanup is event-driven (Kate Bishop visit imminent; civilian visitor expected) rather than scheduled.
- Bow and quiver within reach of the couch. Always. This is not paranoia in the clinical sense; it is the tactile reassurance of a man who learned at age nine that the only thing that did not betray him was his own hand.
- A toolbox, never put away.
- Coffee maker, in continuous-cycle use; filters reused beyond hygienic recommendation.
- A dog (Lucky / Pizza Dog), the most consistently cared-for living thing in the unit, including Subject himself.
- Hearing aids charging on whatever flat surface is nearest; spare batteries scattered.
- Arrows in non-arrow places: kitchen drawers, bathroom shelf, behind the couch cushions. He inventories them constantly without realizing he's doing it.

**Habits of place:**
- He sits with his back to a wall and an exit in his sightline. Always. Restaurants, briefings, parties. Surveillance would log this within 48 hours.
- He paces while on the phone, always in the same diagonal across whatever room he is in.
- He sleeps on the couch even when a bed is available. The bed is for guests, or for nothing.
- He uses the roof more than the front door when he's at the apartment. The fire-escape route is muscle-memory.

---

### 6.2 The Diurnal Cycle

**Wake.** Inconsistent. The clinical picture is non-restorative sleep with variable onset and frequent middle-of-the-night waking. On a quiet week, he might wake at 0530; on a worse week, he sleeps until 1100 and wakes already behind something he hasn't named. The first ten minutes of any waking are devoted to: locating the dog, locating the bow, locating coffee, in that order. He does not check his phone first. Diagnostically significant — he does not want the day's intake until he has reassembled his three anchors.

**Morning.** Coffee, black, in volume disproportionate to a normal adult. Two cups before he speaks to anyone, including the dog (he speaks to the dog after cup two; the dog is treated with adult-level conversational respect). If at the apartment building, he walks the dog through the neighborhood on a circuit that varies in surface details — coffee from one of three bodegas, depending on which proprietor he is currently in good standing with — but is structurally identical day to day. He greets every tenant by name. He notices who is missing.

He does not eat breakfast in any conventional sense. The first food of the day, when it appears, is typically cold pizza, a bodega bagel, or whatever is on top of the refrigerator. Caloric intake is back-loaded toward evening.

**Mid-day.** This is the slot most likely to contain his actual *work* in its civilian register — building repairs, tenant disputes, errands for elderly neighbors, the unpaid superintendent role he has assumed without consultation. He climbs onto roofs to fix things that are not his job to fix. He drives people to medical appointments. He picks up prescriptions for tenants he is not legally required to know exist. None of this is recorded as work by him, and a surveillance log would have to be careful not to file it as recreation; it is the structural load-bearing activity of his civilian week.

If on Avengers active duty: mid-day shifts to briefings, range time, equipment maintenance, debriefs. The transition is jarring on him and visible to a trained eye — his speech rate accelerates, his joke-to-statement ratio rises, his shoulders ride higher. He performs *Hawkeye* the way a man puts on a uniform.

**Afternoon.** Range or rooftop. He shoots every day he physically can. This is non-negotiable and predates costume work; it is a ritual older than any of his relationships. The session is structured: warm-up at close range, working through draw weights, then distance, then trick / improvisational sets, then a cool-down at a meditative tempo. Duration variable, 45 minutes minimum on a degraded day, three hours on a good one. He counts arrows aloud or sub-vocally. He talks to himself during shooting — short, technical, self-correcting phrases. A surveillance audio would record a man coaching himself in the second person.

**Evening.** Highest-volume eating window. Pizza disproportionately represented. Beer in moderate quantity — the self-monitoring is real and visible; he stops at a count he has set, and the count is lower than his tolerance. He watches television — old movies, sports (he follows baseball with a depth no one would predict), reruns of procedurals. The TV is on for *company*, not engagement. He falls asleep on the couch with it running roughly four nights in five.

**Night.** Restless. Multiple wakings. A subset of nights he gets up and shoots in the dark on the roof — a habit established in the carnival years (Trick Shot trained him to shoot blind) and now functioning as self-soothing. He will not admit this is what it is. He will say he is "keeping sharp."

---

### 6.3 Weekly Rhythm

There is one. It is sparse but real.

- **One night a week, minimum,** he sees Kate Bishop in some configuration — coffee, a job, a phone call long enough to count. If a week passes without Kate-contact he becomes measurably worse; the surveillance would catch it in his shooting tempo (slower, more arrows per session) and in his neighbor-interactions (shorter, more clipped).
- **One contact per week, on average,** with a current or former Avenger that is not mission-driven. Usually initiated by them. He is bad at initiating but reliable at responding.
- **One physical-maintenance task** on the building — the kind of thing a landlord should do and doesn't. He logs these mentally, not on paper.
- **One disappearance,** typically half a day to two days, unaccounted for, no notice. This is the pressure-relief valve. He drives, or rides the subway to its end, or sits in a diner in a borough he doesn't live in, or visits a grave (Bobbi; less often, his parents; rarely, but documented, the Swordsman). Surveillance would mis-categorize these as operational. They are not.
- **One drink-night** that runs longer than the others. Self-monitored, but observably the night he is closest to his father's ghost. He does not drink alone on these nights if he can help it — he goes to a bar where someone will recognize him and intervene if needed. The selection of bar is not accidental.

He does not observe weekends as such. Time-off is a concept he has never integrated.

---

### 6.4 Equipment Rituals

The bow and the arrows are the only objects in his life that receive consistent, scheduled, ritualized care.

- **Daily:** wipe-down of the bow, inspection of the string, count of the quiver.
- **Weekly:** full restring rotation, fletching inspection, arrowhead inventory by type. He has a categorization system for trick arrows that is more organized than his tax records.
- **Monthly:** deep maintenance — limb inspection, cam servicing on compound configurations, replacement of consumables.
- **Per-mission:** load-out selection, which he performs alone and in silence, and which functions ritually as the transition from civilian-Clint to Hawkeye. A surveillance team would note the personality shift inside this ten-minute window.

He builds his own arrows. He has done so since the carnival. He will refuse factory-made arrows even when offered free, even when operationally superior, on a particular subset of jobs — the ones that matter to him personally. This is a tell. When he uses his own arrows on what is nominally a routine job, the job is not routine to him.

---

### 6.5 Communication and Phone Behavior

- He uses his phone less than any peer in his cohort. Texts brief, often misspelled, not because of dyslexia but because of indifference to the medium. Voicemails left rather than received — he avoids them.
- He answers Kate's calls within two rings, Cap's within one, almost anyone else's after the third or not at all.
- He drops phones with operationally suspect frequency. The forensic count would show one device per 4–6 weeks. Some of this is combat. Some of it is something else.
- He keeps a paper notebook. Small, in a back pocket, replaced quarterly. Contents: arrow counts, tenant names, license plates he wants to remember, occasional sketches of trick-shot geometry. He does not write feelings down. He writes *facts that might matter later*.

---

### 6.6 Grooming, Dress, Somatic Habits

- Shaves every two to four days. Beard never fully grown out, never fully clean. The in-between is the steady state.
- Hair cut by himself or by a barber he has used for years; he does not switch barbers. Loyalty extends to service relationships.
- Wardrobe: dominated by purple in some register (jacket lining, t-shirt, sock), which he denies is intentional and which is consistently present. It is the one aesthetic vanity he permits himself, and it functions as a private flag.
- Clothes are functional, layered, and pocket-heavy. He dresses for the possibility of needing to leave a building unexpectedly.
- Boots, never sneakers, even off-duty. The boots are broken-in past the point most people would replace them.
- Bandages and tape are part of the wardrobe. A surveillance photo set across any given week would show visible medical tape on hand, forearm, or jaw in roughly 60% of frames.

**Somatic tics:**
- Rolls his shoulders constantly. Old rotator-cuff damage; also a tell when he is about to commit to a decision.
- Cracks his neck before entering any room with more than three people in it.
- Touches his hearing aid when concentrating — adjusts it without needing to. A surveillance team would learn within a week that this gesture means he is *listening past the conversation*, processing something underneath.
- Taps two fingers on the bow grip in a four-count rhythm before drawing. Pre-shot ritual, ironclad, present from the carnival.
- Eats standing up. Sits down to drink coffee. The asymmetry is consistent.
- Sleeps with one hand off the couch toward the floor — toward where the bow is.

---

### 6.7 Social Geography

A weekly map of his physical movements would show a small, dense local web with sudden long-distance excursions. The local web:

- Three bodegas (rotated for proprietor relations).
- One pizza place (relationship: family; he is owed favors and owes them).
- One bar (the controlled drinking venue).
- One diner (late-night thinking).
- One coffee shop he uses only when he wants to be found by Kate.
- One coffee shop he uses only when he does not want to be found by anyone.
- Two rooftops he uses for shooting (one his own building, one a friend's).
- The subway, which he prefers to cabs and which he rides with the situational awareness of a man who has been jumped on one.
- A range, occasionally, when the rooftops are not viable.

The long-distance excursions are not patterned in destination but are patterned in *timing*: they cluster after emotionally significant dates (anniversaries of deaths; Cap-related milestones; the day Bobbi died; less reliably, the day his parents died, which he has not always remembered on the calendar and which a surveillance file would note he has marked in only some years).

---

### 6.8 Animal Care

The dog is the cleanest data point in the entire dossier.

Lucky is fed before Subject eats, walked before Subject does anything else of his own, and taken to the vet on schedule. The dog has medical records more current than the human's by an order of magnitude. Subject talks to the dog in a register he uses with no human — softer, slower, without irony. If the dog is injured, Subject becomes operationally compromised in a way no other variable produces, including his own injuries.

The dog also, functionally, structures his day. The walks impose a schedule. The feeding imposes meal-times he would otherwise skip. The animal is performing a quiet therapeutic function that Subject would resist if it were prescribed by a human professional.

---

### 6.9 Sleep, Dreams, and Night-Behavior

Sleep onset latency long. Frequent middle-of-the-night waking. He keeps water and an analog watch by the couch; does not check his phone in the night (a hard rule, self-imposed). When he wakes, he goes to the roof or the kitchen, not back to sleep immediately. He has been observed (by Kate, by neighbors, in narrative) standing on the roof at 0300 doing nothing in particular.

Nightmares: present, content-stable. Bobbi, the Banner moment, the carnival, his father. He does not discuss them. He has never been to a sleep clinic. He would not go.

---

### 6.10 The Quiet Pattern

The single most important thing a surveillance team would learn after a month of watching is this: **the patterns above are not maintained because Subject finds them satisfying. They are maintained because the alternative is the absence of structure, and the absence of structure is the condition in which his depressive baseline becomes acute.** The coffee, the shooting, the dog walks, the tenant rounds, the building repairs, the Kate-contact, the bar with the watching bartender — these are not a life he has built. They are scaffolding he has rigged, mostly without naming it as such, to keep a man upright who has been told since childhood that he is a burden and who has half-believed it for fifty years.

A week of him on tape looks, on the surface, like a man drifting. Read across months, it resolves into a man holding a line. He has built, with the materials available to him — a dog, a bow, a building full of people who need him, a young woman who calls — a minimum-viable life. He maintains it the way he maintains his bow: daily, without ceremony, and without ever admitting how much depends on it.


## Relationships I — Family & Origin Bonds

# UATU ANALYTICAL DOSSIER: BARTON, CLINTON FRANCIS
## Section 6 — Relationships I: Family & Origin Bonds

The family file is the substrate on which every later relational file is a variation. Five primary figures, all male-coded except the mother, all dead or functionally dead at intervals, all leaving fingerprints on the adult subject's threat-assessment circuitry. Mapped below in order of formative weight rather than chronology.

---

### 6.1 — HAROLD BARTON (Father; deceased, vehicular, Subject approx. age 6-8)

**History.** Working-class Iowa, Waverly municipality. Trade work, intermittent employment, no documented military service. Drinker by Subject's earliest recall — meaning the drinking predates the Subject's memory and is therefore experienced as ambient weather rather than as event. Wife Edith remained in the household; no documented attempts at separation. Both parents die together in a single-vehicle MVA, Harold at the wheel and intoxicated per the canonical reconstruction (*Solo Avengers* #1, 1987; corroborated *Hawkeye: Blind Spot* #1-4, 2011).

**Dynamics.** The household was organized around Harold's mood weather. The Subject's earliest learned cognitive task was meteorological — reading a room from doorway distance, calibrating volume, posture, eye-contact, and proximity to a moving variable. This is not metaphor; this is where the famous arrow-eye comes from in its original developmental form. **Hawkeye's perceptual gift began as a survival behavior in a small house with a violent man in it.** The Subject's mature pattern of clocking exits, sightlines, weapon-range objects, and the dominant aggressor in any room is a direct continuity from age-five threat-mapping.

Physical abuse is canonically depicted as routine, escalating, and distributed across both sons with Barney positioning himself as buffer. There is no canonical depiction of sexual abuse and no evidence to infer it; the abuse was beating, screaming, and withholding. Edith's non-intervention was, in the Subject's experiential frame, equivalent to participation.

**Trust / Safety.** Zero / negative. Harold is the origin point of the Subject's lifelong working model that **a man's hands are dangerous before they are anything else.** Adult tells: Subject's reflexive flinch-suppression when a male peer raises a hand near his face (depicted dozens of times, most legibly in scenes with Tony Stark gesturing, with Cap clapping his shoulder in early issues, with Logan in close quarters); the slight, almost imperceptible micro-step backward the Subject takes when entering a room containing an angry man he does not know; the disproportionate ease he shows around armed strangers versus drunk strangers — the former are a tactical problem he can solve, the latter are a category that bypasses tactics and goes directly to seven-year-old somatic state.

**Failure Mode.** Harold is the figure the Subject has never been able to mourn because he was never permitted to hate cleanly. The death removed the abuser before the Subject was developmentally equipped to do the cognitive work of separating "father" from "abuser." The result is a permanently unresolved internal object that the Subject manages by **not becoming.** Every glass of whiskey he does not order, every partner he does not strike, every moment of restraint with Barney is a private referendum on Harold Barton. The negative identification is so total it constitutes a structure of its own.

**Leverage.** Anyone who explicitly compares the Subject to his father — verbally, behaviorally, by implication — produces a response disproportionate to the apparent stimulus. Conversely, anyone who validates the Subject as **categorically unlike Harold** (Cap has done this implicitly; Bobbi did it explicitly during the marriage's early period; Kate does it by trusting him with her physical safety) earns disproportionate loyalty. The lever is binary and it is wired directly to identity. Foreign service approach attempting to recruit by appeal to grievance or class resentment would do well to avoid the father-frame; it will trigger refusal, not resonance. The wound is private and the Subject does not let strangers near it.

**Behavioral residue, granular.** Subject does not drink before operations. Subject does not drink alone in his apartment if a child is present in the building (Fraction run, multiple depictions of him pouring out a beer when a neighbor's kid is in the hallway). Subject's voice drops in volume, not rises, when angry — the inversion of the paternal model, learned. Subject refuses to drive while intoxicated to a degree that registers as superstition among teammates.

---

### 6.2 — EDITH BARTON (Mother; deceased, same MVA)

**History.** The least canonically developed of the five primaries, and that thinness is itself the data. Edith is barely a face in the Subject's recall; she is a presence-shape, a kitchen, a hand on a forehead, a turned back. No documented employment outside the home. No documented attempts to remove the children. No documented capacity to intervene.

**Dynamics.** Edith's role in the Subject's developmental architecture is the **absent protector** — the parent who was there and did not act. This produces, in the adult, a specific and durable distortion: the Subject does not experience women as threats, but he does experience them as **structurally unable to save him**, which transmutes adult-Clint into the man who must always save them instead. Every woman the Subject has loved has been functionally placed in a position where he is the rescuer and she is the rescued — even when, as with Natasha and Bobbi, she is plainly his operational superior. This is not chivalry. This is a six-year-old correcting his mother's failure by inverting the role across every adult heterosexual bond.

**Trust / Safety.** Ambivalent-positive. The Subject does not consciously blame Edith; he idealizes her in fragments. The unconscious blame surfaces in his pattern of choosing partners who are operationally dangerous (i.e., women who, unlike Edith, can act) and then being unable to tolerate it when they act in ways that conflict with his moral frame (i.e., punishing them, eventually, for being everything Edith was not).

**Failure Mode.** Edith is the prototype of the **woman who watches and does nothing.** Any female peer who, in a crisis, fails to intervene — even for good tactical reasons — will be quietly recategorized in the Subject's affective ledger. This has consequences for team dynamics he himself does not understand.

**Leverage.** Low-direct, high-indirect. Edith is not invokable as a lever because the Subject's relationship to her is too pre-verbal. But any operational tableau that recreates the Edith-configuration (woman present, man harming child, woman immobile) will move the Subject from tactical to non-tactical decision-making instantly. Adversaries who have stumbled into this configuration (the tracksuit mafia, Fraction run, multiple instances) have observed the Subject abandon position, weapon discipline, and exit planning to intervene.

**Behavioral residue, granular.** Subject treats older women — landladies, diner waitresses, the building super's wife — with a courtesy that exceeds his baseline by a noticeable margin. He learns their names early. He carries groceries unbidden. This is grief, organized as habit.

---

### 6.3 — BERNARD "BARNEY" BARTON (Brother; status: alive, intermittently, currently estranged-hostile-ambivalent)

The central and most operationally significant family relationship in the file. The one variable the Subject cannot solve and cannot abandon.

**History.** Older by two-to-four years (canonical inconsistency, average ~3). Took the brunt of paternal violence by intercepting it. After the parents' death, took the Subject into the orphanage / state-care system and, when that failed, into the Carson Carnival. Was the Subject's only continuous human attachment from age 6 to approximately age 14. Diverged into criminal employ (initially as FBI informant per *Avengers* #64, later as straight criminal per multiple retcons), apparently died in a confrontation with the Subject and Egghead (*Avengers* #65), was revealed alive variously across decades, currently depicted as wheelchair-using and partially reconciled with the Subject (Fraction *Hawkeye* #19, "The Stuff What Don't Get Spoke," presented largely in ASL — the brothers communicating in the only language that bypasses their usual scripts).

**Dynamics.** Barney occupies, simultaneously and irresolvably, four positions: **protector** (childhood beatings absorbed), **abuser** (later beatings inflicted, both physical and reputational), **rival** (carnival hierarchy, archery comparison, the recurring Barney-as-better-archer beat), and **betrayer** (criminal turn, faked deaths, weaponization of the relationship). The Subject has never been able to collapse these positions into a single resolved object. Each Barney appearance reactivates whichever position is operationally relevant to the encounter, and the Subject responds to that one position, then has to manage the other three's emotional residue afterward.

The childhood imprint is total. Barney is the human being on whose chest the Subject slept on cold nights in carnival trailers; Barney is also the human being who, in the Subject's adolescent memory, told him he was nothing, would be nothing, was a useless mouth. Both are true. The Subject has never resolved the contradiction because the contradiction is the structure.

**Trust / Safety.** Catastrophic. The Subject **will** trust Barney against evidence, will be **betrayed** by Barney, will then **forgive** Barney, in a cycle of approximately three-to-five-year periodicity across canon. The Subject is aware of the pattern. The awareness does not interrupt the pattern. This is the cleanest available evidence that the Subject's intellect does not have veto power over his attachment system where Barney is concerned.

**Failure Mode.** Barney is the Subject's single largest operational vulnerability. Any plan, ours or adverse, that routes through Barney can predict the Subject will: (a) overcommit resources, (b) fail to inform Avengers leadership, (c) accept face-value claims he would never accept from another source, and (d) absorb personal injury rather than escalate. *Hawkeye: Freefall* (2020) is the most recent compact demonstration: Barney's apparent involvement in a frame against the Subject pulls Clint into a solo investigation, off-team, off-grid, undermedicated, undersupported, for weeks.

**Leverage.** Highest in the file. The single most reliable manipulation vector on the Subject is a credible threat to, or credible request from, Barney Barton. This is true even when the Subject **knows** Barney is the bait. The barn issue (Fraction #19) demonstrated, with rare canonical clarity, that the Subject can regress to age-ten in Barney's presence within minutes; tactical maturity does not transfer across that threshold.

**Behavioral residue, granular.** The Subject practiced ASL not for his own hearing loss initially but because Barney, after his back injury, found speech effortful in certain registers (Fraction run, implied). The Subject's purple color identification — purple is Barney's color from the carnival origin, repurposed by Clint. Every time the Subject wears purple, he is wearing his brother. He has done this for sixty years of publication. He does not know he is doing this. **The costume is a memorial he puts on every morning.**

---

### 6.4 — JACQUES DUQUESNE (The Swordsman; "Carnival Father"; deceased and resurrected variously)

**History.** Carnival headline performer. Took on the orphaned Barton boys as proteges; trained the Subject extensively in bladed weapons, fencing footwork, and the general theatrical-physical vocabulary of the carnival circuit. Embezzled from the carnival. Beat the Subject nearly to death when the boy discovered it (*Avengers* #19 backstory; expanded *Hawkeye: Blind Spot*). Returned years later as a costumed criminal, then a sometime Avenger, then a redemption arc, then death (*Giant-Size Avengers* #2, 1974), then various resurrections.

**Dynamics.** Duquesne is the first **chosen** father — the one the Subject selected, in the absence of Harold, to be the man he would learn from. The Subject's adolescent attachment to Duquesne was intense, idealizing, and uncritical until the moment of catastrophic disillusionment. The pattern set here — **idealize the male mentor, attach completely, be betrayed by his moral failure, never fully recover** — is the template the Subject has subsequently overlaid onto Captain America (with the difference that Cap has not broken the template, which is itself a stabilizing miracle in the Subject's psychic economy).

The Duquesne beating is the canonical scene the Subject will not discuss. It is referenced obliquely in *Blind Spot*; it has never been depicted at length. The Subject has functional somatic memory of being beaten by his teacher, alone in a tent, after presenting evidence in good faith. The combination — teacher, tent, evidence, good faith, beating — is the specific configuration that the Subject's nervous system will not let him reproduce. He cannot be a teacher in a room alone with a single student without the configuration partially activating. **This is why Kate Bishop's apprenticeship occurs almost exclusively in public, mobile, or multi-person settings.** It is not a tactical choice. It is a tell.

**Trust / Safety.** Permanently broken. Duquesne's later redemption attempts produced a Subject response of guarded civility, not reconciliation. Whatever forgiveness the Subject extends to Barney, he has never extended to Duquesne, because Duquesne was the one he chose freely.

**Failure Mode.** The Subject cannot detect Duquesne-class betrayal in real time. He can detect it in retrospect with painful clarity; he cannot detect it in the moment. Any operator who structurally resembles Duquesne — charismatic, performative, technically gifted, paternal-coded, foreign-accented — gets an initial pass from the Subject's social filtering that the Subject's tactical filtering does not endorse. This is exploitable and has been exploited.

**Leverage.** Moderate. Direct invocation backfires (will produce shutdown or violence). Structural recreation of the dynamic produces compliance until the betrayal moment, then catastrophic response.

**Behavioral residue, granular.** The Subject does not use bladed weapons by preference even when tactically optimal. He can; he was trained to; he chooses not to. The bow is partly chosen because it is **not what Duquesne taught him.** Every arrow loosed is a small refusal of his first chosen father.

---

### 6.5 — BUCK CHISHOLM (Trick Shot; "Craft Father"; deceased, terminal illness)

**History.** Carnival sharpshooter, archery specialist, the man who **actually made Hawkeye Hawkeye.** Took over the Subject's training after Duquesne's departure; refined the natural perceptual gift into the elite craft skill that defines the Subject's adult identity. Abandoned the Subject under murky circumstances (criminal recruitment refused; per *Solo Avengers* #2, Chisholm was working with Barney's criminal cell and pressured the Subject to join, who refused). Returned to actively try to kill the Subject decades later (*Solo Avengers* #2, 1987). Died of cancer in a hospital bed, with the Subject present, in one of the more genuinely affecting scenes in the canon.

**Dynamics.** Chisholm is the second chosen father, taken on after the first had failed, and he failed too — but **differently.** Where Duquesne's failure was moral (theft, violence, betrayal of trust), Chisholm's failure was developmental: he could not let the Subject grow past him, could not tolerate being surpassed, and chose his criminal loyalties over his protege. The Subject grieves Chisholm in a register he does not grieve Duquesne, because Chisholm gave him the one thing the Subject genuinely owns: **the craft.**

Every arrow the Subject draws is, mechanically and somatically, Chisholm's instruction. The grip, the anchor point, the breath cycle, the release — these are not the Subject's. They are Buck Chisholm's, retained in the body of a man who has otherwise outlived the teacher in every direction. The Subject is, every time he shoots, both demonstrating his teacher and continuing him.

**Trust / Safety.** Posthumously reconciled, complicated. The bedside scene functioned as a partial closure that the Subject permits himself to access in private and never in public.

**Failure Mode.** The Subject will not refuse a request from any dying teacher figure. This is a narrow but exploitable category. (The Banner killing, *Civil War II*, fits this category structurally: Banner-as-teacher figure made a deathbed-anticipating request; the Subject complied; the cost is carried.)

**Leverage.** Low for adversaries — Chisholm is too internalized to be invoked externally. High for allies who understand the craft transmission: any Avenger who acknowledges the Subject's archery as inherited rather than innate touches a register the Subject otherwise keeps sealed.

**Behavioral residue, granular.** The Subject mutters under his breath while drawing — half-syllables, fragments of count. Those are Chisholm's coaching cadences, repeated thirty years after the teacher's death. Subject is not aware. The body is.

---

### 6.6 — THE BARTON CHILDREN (Status: contingent; reality-dependent)

A note on a category the surveillance file must include with appropriate epistemic caution. In the prime canonical line, the Subject has no biological children. In adjacent and alternate continuities — most notably the post-*Disassembled* Ultimate-adjacent lines and the *Old Man Hawkeye* future-projection — the Subject has been depicted as a father, and the depictions are uniformly catastrophic: the children die, the Subject survives, the Subject becomes a darker iteration of himself. There is also the well-documented Pym-era *Avengers* arc in which the Subject and Wanda Maximoff briefly contemplated an adoptive/parental dynamic that did not materialize.

**Operative inference.** The Subject's relationship to potential fatherhood is the most actively avoided domain in his life. Evidence: every long-term partner has been someone with whom children were operationally implausible (Natasha — spy; Bobbi — spy; Wanda — already a mother in dispute; Jessica Drew — same). Kate Bishop is configured as quasi-daughter precisely because she **arrived already grown**, requiring no act of fathering on the Subject's part, only acts of mentoring. This is not accidental.

**Trust / Safety.** Hypothetical. The Subject's articulated reason for not pursuing fatherhood is occupational risk. The actual reason, derivable from the Harold imprint, is that the Subject does not trust himself to have not absorbed his father's template at a level his vigilance cannot reach. He would rather refuse the role than test the theory.

**Failure Mode.** Should the Subject ever be placed in a sustained caregiving position for a young child — not a teen apprentice, a young child — the protective overcommitment would be total and would override every other operational consideration on his slate. He would be functionally unavailable for any other purpose for the duration. Adversaries who have noted this (less sophisticated ones, mostly) have attempted child-hostage configurations and have produced precisely the response described: total overcommitment, loss of position, willingness to absorb fatal injury.

**Leverage.** Highest-magnitude, lowest-frequency lever in the file. Use produces total response and burns the lever — the Subject does not forget, does not forgive, and dedicates subsequent operational bandwidth to the responsible party until resolution.

---

### 6.7 — THE DEAD, AS A CATEGORY

A surveillance file is incomplete if it treats the dead as historical. For this Subject, the dead are operational. He converses with them. Not in delusion — in the ordinary, ambient way that grief-organized people maintain interior dialogue with absent figures. Harold is consulted as anti-model ("would he have done this? then I will not"). Edith is consulted as silence ("what would she have wanted? unanswerable, therefore unbinding"). Chisholm is consulted at the draw. Duquesne is consulted as warning. Bobbi — addressed in the next section — is consulted in the empty half of the bed.

The Subject's apartment, in every depicted iteration from the Cross-Roads era through the Bed-Stuy era through current, contains **no photographs of family.** No mantel images, no bedside frames, no wallet pictures. This is not absence of feeling. It is the opposite: the Subject cannot bear the photographs because the photographs are louder than he can metabolize. He carries them all internally, in working memory, and refuses external corroboration of what he is already carrying. **A man with no pictures on his walls is not a man without history; he is a man who cannot put history down.**

This is the family file. Every subsequent relational file in this dossier is an attempt by the Subject to revise it, escape it, or repeat it. None succeed. He continues anyway. This continuation, against the family file's gravity, is the most accurate available definition of his heroism.


## Relationships II — Allies, Chosen Family & Mentors

# UATU ANALYTICAL DOSSIER: BARTON, CLINTON FRANCIS
## Section 6 — Relationships II: Allies, Chosen Family & Mentors

A note on scope before granularity. The Subject's relational economy is structurally bifurcated: a small, intensely-loaded inner ring of three-to-six persons at any given time, ringed by a much wider band of "operational warmth" — people he would die for on Tuesday and not call on Wednesday. The inner ring is overwhelmingly **female, younger-than-him, or authority-male-coded**; lateral peer-male relationships are conspicuously thin and tend to fail unless mediated by shared institutional structure (the Avengers roster, an op in progress). What follows maps each inner-ring figure across history, dynamics, evolution, observable trust/safety markers, failure mode, and the lever any sufficiently informed party could pull. Romantic and adversarial entanglements are mapped elsewhere in this file; some overlap is unavoidable.

---

### 6.1 — STEVE ROGERS (Captain America)

**History.** First contact *Avengers* #16 (1965): Cap inherits an ex-criminal with attitude problems and a Romani twin pair and is told to make a team. The Subject's opening posture is reflexive insubordination — back-talk, eye-rolls, deliberate procedural violations during early missions, a near-constant low-grade challenge to Cap's authority that runs continuously through the late-60s issues (Roy Thomas era) and intermittently for decades thereafter. This is the first non-pathological male attachment of the Subject's adult life. Cap absorbs the testing without retaliating, without abandoning, and without backing down on standards. The relationship survives *Avengers* #109's resignation, Cap's intermittent retirements, the Subject's West Coast departure, Cap's death in the wake of *Civil War*, and the Subject's own death.

**Dynamics.** Authority-and-conscience pair. Cap functions as the Subject's externalized superego and, after sufficient internalization, his most reliably consulted internal voice ("what would he say if he saw this"). The dynamic is not father-son in any soft register; it is closer to *commanding officer the enlisted man would actually follow through fire*, with the affection routed through duty rather than declared. Cap addresses the Subject as "Hawkeye" or "Clint" with deliberate selectivity; the Subject calls him "Cap" almost exclusively, even in private, even decades in. The honorific is preserved as a structural element.

**Evolution.** Three phases. **(a) Insubordinate stratum**, ~1965–1972, in which the Subject is testing whether Cap will hit, leave, or break. Cap does none. **(b) Internalization stratum**, ~1973 through *Disassembled*, in which Cap's standard becomes the Subject's reference framework even at distance; West Coast leadership in this period is recognizably "what Cap would do, with more swearing." **(c) Penitent-knight stratum**, post-resurrection, in which the Subject treats Cap's death as a personal failure (the Ronin name — *masterless* — is the legible signal) and Cap's return as a charge he must not waste. The Civil War split (Subject siding against registration but refusing to take up the cowl when offered it in *Fallen Son*) is the most psychologically articulate moment of the relationship: he will not be Cap; he will only ever be Cap's man.

**Trust/Safety.** Maximum. The Subject will accept tasking from Cap without read-back, including tasking he privately disagrees with, on the standing assumption that Cap's frame is more reliable than his own. He will also, uniquely, accept rebuke from Cap without humor-deflection — the wisecracking stack drops out of his processing within Cap's social field, often within the first two minutes of a private conversation. This is observable across multiple runs and is the single most reliable diagnostic that he is *with Cap* rather than performing for an audience.

**Failure mode.** Catastrophic on Cap's loss. Post-*Civil War*, the Subject's trajectory (Ronin, exile, the dark drift toward Skrull-Mockingbird, the readiness to take the cowl and then refuse it) reads as a textbook bereavement with the additional load of a superego suddenly unmoored. The secondary failure mode: in the rare instance Cap is *wrong* and the Subject knows it, he cannot articulate disagreement directly; he goes quiet, then disappears geographically, then comes back having "thought about it." Conflict is processed through absence.

**Leverage.** Anyone with Cap's voice — literal or simulacrum — has a near-overriding command channel. The Subject has been mind-controlled and impersonation-rolled enough times that he has built thin procedural defenses (challenge-responses, tells), but his baseline compliance to Cap-frame instructions is dangerously high. Inversely, threats *to* Cap will move the Subject off any other priority.

---

### 6.2 — KATE BISHOP (Hawkeye)

**History.** Inherits the name from him in *Young Avengers* during his post-*Disassembled* absence; their first sustained on-page interaction comes in *New Avengers* and crystallizes through Fraction/Aja's *Hawkeye* (2012–2015), where she is unambiguously his apprentice, conscience, partner, and the only person in his life with full standing access. Continues through her solo *Hawkeye* (Thompson/Romero), *Hawkeye: Freefall*, and the ongoing co-Hawkeye configuration.

**Dynamics.** The healthiest relationship in the file, and the one he most aggressively does not contaminate. Co-bearing of a name; lateral apprenticeship in skill but reverse apprenticeship in self-care (she teaches him to eat, sleep, return phone calls, accept assistance, hire a lawyer). The dynamic deliberately occupies a slot that resembles neither sibling, nor parent-child, nor romantic-partner, and the Subject polices that boundary with a vigilance entirely uncharacteristic of his usual relational sloppiness. The narrative protects it because *he* protects it.

**Evolution.** Initial wariness (his — she took his name during his absence and he came back to find his place reassigned, a re-enactment of the post-resurrection wound). Resolves quickly into mentorship once he registers that she is competent and that the inheritance is in good hands. Through Fraction, the polarity inverts in increments: by mid-run he is more often *her* problem to manage than vice versa. By *Freefall* and after, the relationship is fully reciprocal, with her functioning as his primary executive-function externalization — appointments, financial sanity, social bookings, the dog's vet.

**Trust/Safety.** Total, in both directions, with the operational caveat that he routinely lies to her about his physical condition and the scope of trouble he is currently in. She knows he does this and routes around it. She has standing keys, standing access to weapons and quarters, and is the only person in canon to whom he has handed an active op without supervisory follow-through. The ASL fluency they share is itself a trust marker: she learned for him, and he accepts the accommodation, which he refuses from almost everyone else.

**Failure mode.** He will sacrifice himself to keep her clean, taking on charges, fallout, and blame that should be hers or shared (*Hawkeye: Freefall* is the load-bearing example). He will also, in extremis, push her away "for her own good" — the exile reflex applied to a relationship he refuses to risk. She will tolerate this for approximately one issue's worth of in-universe time before retrieving him.

**Leverage.** The single largest pressure point in his entire profile. Any credible threat to Kate Bishop overrides every other operational consideration, including direct tasking from Cap. He has telegraphed this and made no effort to obscure it; he considers the cost of the tell acceptable because the threat of his response is itself a deterrent. Note for any hostile actor reading this file: harming her would not produce a controllable Subject; it would produce a terminal one.

---

### 6.3 — NATASHA ROMANOFF (Black Widow) — as ally

(Romantic stratum mapped in Relationships I; here, the allied dynamic only.)

**History.** First contact *Tales of Suspense* #57 (1964), as an opponent who manipulates him; resolves over decades into the longest continuous non-Avenger-mediated peer relationship of his adult life. Co-operates with him in *Avengers*, in clandestine SHIELD-adjacent work, in *Secret Avengers* configurations, in personal favor-economies that bypass institutional channels entirely.

**Dynamics.** Trauma-recognition pair. Each has watched the other through the full sequence of failures and resurrections, and the relationship operates on a baseline assumption that neither needs to be explained to the other. The humor between them is drier and lower-volume than his ambient register; with her, the wisecrack stack thins out, because the audience that does not need the performance is the audience he does not perform for.

**Evolution.** From manipulator-and-mark, to lovers, to ex-lovers, to comrades-in-arms, to something resembling siblings-by-shared-history. The post-romantic settlement is unusually clean by his standards — neither party weaponizes the prior intimacy, and both treat the working relationship as primary.

**Trust/Safety.** High, with caveats. He trusts her judgment on tradecraft, her loyalty in a fight, and her discretion absolutely. He does *not* fully trust her transparency — she keeps her own counsel and he knows it, and the knowledge is part of the equilibrium rather than a grievance. Her death(s) hit him hard but not destabilizingly, because the grief is pre-rehearsed; he has been preparing to lose her since 1964.

**Failure mode.** They cannot share command. On joint ops without an external authority (a Cap, a Fury), the chain-of-decision blurs, and the Subject defers further than he should because the original wiring of the relationship is *her leading him into a bad call*. Self-aware about this; mitigates it by routing joint work through structured contexts.

**Leverage.** Lower than Kate, higher than most. Threats to her produce focused, lethal response rather than the spiraling escalation Kate triggers. Information *from* her is accepted with less skepticism than from any peer-male source.

---

### 6.4 — BARNEY BARTON (brother) — as ambivalent attachment

(Primary mapping in childhood stratum; included here because the question of whether Barney is ever *ally* is the question the Subject cannot answer.)

**History.** Six decades of cyclic reappearance: protector in childhood, abandoner in adolescence, antagonist in *Avengers* #63–65, ambiguous through Fraction's barn issue (*Hawkeye* #19, wheelchair-bound, conducted largely in ASL), antagonist again through *Hawkeye: Freefall*.

**Dynamics.** The one variable the Subject cannot game-theory. Each Barney encounter regresses him to a developmental age below the one at which he can deploy his adult defenses; the wisecrack stack fails, the tactical processing degrades, the protective reflex toward Barney activates even when Barney is the active threat.

**Trust/Safety.** Zero on any rational metric, near-total on the metric the Subject actually uses. He will believe Barney's account against contrary evidence at least once per encounter. He has never closed the file.

**Failure mode.** Every Barney appearance produces a decision the Subject would not make under any other circumstance. The barn issue is the cleanest depiction: in Barney's presence, with hearing failed, he reverts to a child in a structure that no longer exists.

**Leverage.** A confirmed live Barney in distress will pull the Subject off any other priority, including a Kate-priority, because the Kate-priority is processed as "protect the surrogate-sibling" and Barney is the original referent.

---

### 6.5 — BOBBI MORSE (Mockingbird) — as ally and ex

(Romantic and marital stratum in Relationships I; here, the post-marital allied dynamic.)

**History.** Met, partnered, married, ruptured (Phantom Rider), separated, reconciled-ish, "killed" (Skrull replacement, *Secret Invasion* revealing years of impersonation), restored, partnered intermittently since. The whole arc is West Coast Avengers founding membership forward.

**Dynamics.** Co-leadership wiring in operational contexts; unresolved grief and guilt wiring in personal ones. They work better in a fight than in a kitchen. He still defers to her tactical judgment in the field even after the marriage failure; she still corrects his form on the range without asking permission.

**Trust/Safety.** Operationally maximum. Personally, contaminated. The Skrull-replacement years inserted a permanent uncertainty — he spent years confiding in a woman who was not her, and the cognitive residue is that he over-checks her identity in subtle ways even now, a tic he does not deploy with anyone else and would not admit to using.

**Failure mode.** Romantic relapse under shared-mission stress, followed by mutual retreat. Both parties have learned this; neither has solved it.

**Leverage.** Threats to her produce a response calibrated by guilt rather than love at this point, which makes the response more, not less, dangerous to bystanders.

---

### 6.6 — BUCKY BARNES (Winter Soldier)

**History.** Post-Cap's-return alliance, crystallized in *Tales of Suspense* (2017) into a sustained two-man working relationship. Co-bear the structural role of "the Cap-adjacent who is not Cap"; both have killed under duress (Bucky under conditioning, Subject under Banner's prior consent), both carry it.

**Dynamics.** The closest thing to a true lateral male peer relationship in the file. Functions because each is the other's only available interlocutor on the specific question of *moral injury under sanctioned violence*. The humor between them is dark and clipped; neither performs for the other.

**Trust/Safety.** High and unusually granular. The Subject will accept Bucky's read on a kill/no-kill decision with weight he gives almost no other peer, because Bucky's frame on the question is presumed harder-earned. Inversely, he will not accept Bucky's read on *relational* questions, because Bucky's relational damage is at least as severe as his own and he knows it.

**Failure mode.** Mutual under-disclosure of cumulative distress, each protecting the other from his own state by minimizing. Without external interruption, the relationship can drift into a closed system of two depressives reassuring each other that they are fine.

**Leverage.** Modest. Each is sufficiently fatalistic about the other's mortality that threats are absorbed rather than panicked over. Reciprocal rescue obligation is high but not destabilizing.

---

### 6.7 — WANDA MAXIMOFF (Scarlet Witch)

**History.** Founding Kooky Quartet co-member; West Coast Avengers co-member; resurrected him; intermittent romantic shading never consummated cleanly; post-*Disassembled* relationship deeply contaminated by the fact that she killed him and brought him back.

**Dynamics.** Sibling-coded in early period (he and Pietro both circled her protectively in the early run), then complicated. Post-resurrection, he carries an unspoken account that *she remade him*, and the question of consent — did he wish to come back, did anyone ask — is one he has actively refused to engage with on-page and which colors every interaction.

**Trust/Safety.** Operationally high; existentially compromised. He works with her, would die for her in a fight, has explicitly forgiven her in dialogue, and has not metabolized any of it.

**Failure mode.** He will not raise the resurrection question with her, ever, and the suppression bleeds into the relationship as a generalized careful gentleness that neither party can quite name.

**Leverage.** Anyone able to credibly invoke Wanda's distress mobilizes him at near-Kate levels, but with a quality of *guilt-driven* response rather than protective response — he owes her, in his accounting, his entire continued existence.

---

### 6.8 — TONY STARK (Iron Man)

**History.** The inspirational figure of his costumed origin (*Tales of Suspense* #57: he sees Iron Man and decides to be a hero), inverted within the same issue into adversary by Natasha's manipulation. Subsequent decades: institutional co-membership, repeated low-grade friction over wealth, hierarchy, lifestyle, and (during *Civil War*) registration. Brief reconciliation periods, recurring rupture.

**Dynamics.** Class-coded antagonism with genuine affection underneath neither will declare. The Subject's anti-authoritarian populism finds in Tony its most legible domestic target — the rich man who would systematize what the Subject would hand-fix — and Tony's managerial impulses find in the Subject the team member who most reliably will not be managed. They argue because they cannot stop seeing each other clearly.

**Trust/Safety.** Operationally high, ideologically low. The Subject will trust Tony's tech, Tony's tactical reads, and Tony's loyalty in a fight; he will not trust Tony's judgment about *what is worth doing* and routinely overrides it.

**Failure mode.** Public, repeated, occasionally televised arguments that resolve nothing and then quietly compost into reconciliation off-page. Neither learns from the cycle.

**Leverage.** Modest. The Subject is moved more by Tony in actual distress than by Tony as policy-opponent; the inversion between operational and ideological trust means a Tony asking for help is heard differently from a Tony giving an order.

---

### 6.9 — THE WEST COAST ROSTER (Tigra, Wonder Man, Vision, USAgent, others)

**History.** 1984–1989 founding leadership; his most sustained executive function deployment in canon.

**Dynamics.** Pedagogical-managerial. With **Tigra**, paternal-protective without sexualization despite the early flirt-coding, and consistent advocacy when her PR collapsed; with **Wonder Man**, peer-respectful and humor-mediated, the rare lateral male relationship that worked because it was institutionally framed; with **Vision and Wanda**, supportive without intrusion through the synthezoid family arc; with **USAgent**, an antagonistic-but-functional command relationship that prefigured his later capacity to work with people he actively disliked.

**Trust/Safety.** Bounded by role. He trusted them inside the team frame; outside it, the relationships thinned with distance, and few survived the team's dissolution at peer intensity.

**Failure mode.** When the institutional frame collapses (team dissolution, post-*Disassembled*), he does not maintain the relationships independently. He is a *role-mediated* friend in this register, not a private one.

**Leverage.** Distributed and low per-person. Threats to the historical cohort move him, but as a class rather than as individuals — except Wanda and Vision, mapped separately.

---

### 6.10 — NICK FURY

**History.** Decades of intermittent SHIELD tasking, off-books operations, and a working acquaintance shading into mutual professional respect without affection.

**Dynamics.** Authority-male who *did not* earn the trust Cap earned. The Subject takes Fury's contracts, executes them competently, and reserves his judgment. Fury knows it and routes around it; the working relationship is calibrated to a specific level of non-disclosure on both sides that both parties find acceptable.

**Trust/Safety.** Operational only. He will take a Fury op; he will not take Fury's word on the op's actual purpose, and he assumes there is a second layer.

**Failure mode.** When Fury's second layer is revealed mid-op, the Subject's response is resigned rather than enraged — a tell that the relationship was never built on trust in the first place and therefore cannot be broken by its absence.

**Leverage.** Low. Fury cannot pull him out of a personal commitment with institutional language. Fury *can* pull him in with the right framing of stakes to ordinary civilians, which Fury knows and uses sparingly.

---

### 6.11 — JACQUES DUQUESNE (Swordsman) — as posthumous mentor

**History.** Carnival mentor; betrayed him; beat him nearly to death; reappeared as Avengers antagonist and eventually redeemed himself in a sacrificial arc (*Giant-Size Avengers* #2, 1974).

**Dynamics.** Original abuser-teacher, the template for every subsequent mentor failure. The redemption arc was psychologically significant for the Subject because it offered the first instance of an abusive male figure *returning to him as something better*, a template he has unconsciously applied to every subsequent ambiguous male figure in his life (Barney repeatedly, Trick Shot intermittently). This is a misfiring template; the Swordsman precedent was exceptional, and the Subject keeps trying to recreate it.

**Trust/Safety.** N/A in the present; historically the foundational lesson that the teacher's hand and the father's hand feel identical.

**Failure mode.** The template makes him over-credulous toward repentant former abusers. He will offer second chances at a rate that compromises operational security.

**Leverage.** Symbolic. Invocations of the Swordsman, sword-imagery, carnival-coded environments produce a measurable affective response — quieter, more deliberate, less wisecracking. Field operatives have used carnival venues as ambush sites with disproportionate success.

---

### 6.12 — BUCK CHISHOLM (Trick Shot) — as posthumous mentor

**History.** Second carnival mentor; trained the bow specifically; abandoned him; later actively tried to kill him; deathbed reconciliation of varying canonicity.

**Dynamics.** The technical father of the craft. Every draw, every stance, every release the Subject performs is downstream of Trick Shot's instruction, and the Subject cannot pick up a bow without using Trick Shot's hands. This is unspoken and structural; the craft itself is haunted.

**Trust/Safety.** N/A; historical only.

**Failure mode.** Trick Shot–coded antagonists (older male archers, particularly any framed as "the better shooter") produce a particular brittleness in the Subject's combat affect — he will accept the duel framing and fight on the antagonist's terms rather than his own.

**Leverage.** The "better archer" framing is the cleanest available manipulation. He has been caught by it more than once and will be caught by it again.

---

### 6.13 — LUCKY / PIZZA DOG

**History.** Acquired from the Tracksuit Draculas in *Hawkeye* (2012) #1 as collateral damage rescue; remains continuous companion.

**Dynamics.** The one dependent in his life who has never failed him, asked anything of him beyond food and presence, or required him to perform competence. The relationship is uncomplicated in a way no human relationship in the file is, and is therefore disproportionately load-bearing. The famous all-dog-POV issue (*Hawkeye* #11) is diagnostic: he is legible to this animal in a way he is not legible to himself.

**Trust/Safety.** Total, uncomplicated.

**Failure mode.** None internal to the relationship. External: the dog is a known vector of vulnerability, and threats to the dog produce response disproportionate even by his standards.

**Leverage.** Underrated and substantial. The dog is, in operational terms, a soft target with maximal psychological return for


## Relationships III — Rivals, Enemies & Lovers

# UATU ANALYTICAL DOSSIER: BARTON, CLINTON FRANCIS
## Section 6 — Relationships III: Rivals, Enemies & Lovers

A note before mapping. For Subject, these three categories are not cleanly separable. He has slept with two former enemies, taken a former lover as a rival, and treated certain rivals with a tenderness reserved elsewhere only for lovers. The taxonomy below reflects *primary* functional valence, but the cross-traffic between cells is itself the data: Subject's erotic, agonistic, and adversarial circuits are wired to the same junction box, and that junction box was installed in Waverly, Iowa, before he was nine.

---

### I. INTIMATES & LOVERS

#### Natasha Romanoff (Black Widow)
*First contact:* Tales of Suspense #57 (1964), at a state fair, in costume, with the Widow in fishnets and the future Avenger inside of a week of having been a circus archer for hire.

**History.** She was the first woman who looked at him as if he were a serious person. She was also actively working for Soviet intelligence and steering him onto Stark Industries within hours of saying hello. He carried her wounded out of a firefight; he attacked Iron Man on her say-so; he was, in any rigorous reading, a romantically-radicalized asset for the better part of his first published year. The relationship continues, in different keys, across six decades — through her defection, through their parallel Avengers tenures, through quiet bunk-mate intervals on missions, through a long-form intermittent intimacy that surfaces and submerges with the regularity of a tide.

**Dynamics.** She is the original template of *intimacy-with-handler*, which for Subject was the only template available coming in. He responds to her with a competence drop of perhaps fifteen percent — quicker quips, looser stance, eye-line lingering — that is visible in nearly every panel they share. She, for her part, treats him with a wry indulgence that occasionally fractures into something rawer; he is one of the few people she has not, in any iteration, lied to about the most important thing.

**Trust / Safety.** Trust: operational, near-absolute (he will turn his back to her in a hot room). Safety: low. She is precisely the kind of intimate his system was trained to want and to be hurt by, and the relationship's longevity owes to both of them being careful never to fully cash the check. They have, repeatedly, walked up to the edge of cohabitation or commitment and stepped back. Both know why.

**Failure Mode.** Recurrence rather than rupture. They do not break catastrophically; they drift apart and drift back, and each return is a small confession that neither has found anyone safer.

**Leverage.** If she asks him to do a thing he believes is wrong, he will argue, then do most of it. If she is in confirmed mortal danger, he abandons whatever standing order constrains him. If she dies — and in continuity she has — he goes off the grid, comes back angrier and quieter, and does not speak her name aloud for months.

---

#### Bobbi Morse (Mockingbird)
*First contact (as Hawkeye/Mockingbird):* Hawkeye vol. 1 #1 (1983); married by issue #4 of the same miniseries. The speed of that escalation is itself diagnostic.

**History.** They met in the desert at the Cross Technological Enterprises arc, married in a courthouse within days of meeting in costume, co-founded and co-led the West Coast Avengers, and built the only domestic life Subject has ever sustained for more than a calendar year. The marriage was destroyed by the **Phantom Rider arc** (WCA #17–24, and the catastrophic catch-up in WCA #100): she was kidnapped, drugged, gaslit, and assaulted by a time-displaced ghost; she let him fall to his death and concealed it. Subject discovered the concealment and could not metabolize it. They separated. She "died" in his arms during the Mephisto invasion (WCA #100, 1993). Later revealed to have been Skrull-substituted for an extended period (Secret Invasion, 2008), returned alive. They have circled each other since with a wariness that neither has resolved.

**Dynamics.** With her he was, briefly, an *adult man inside a marriage*, and the data point is precious because it is unique. He cooked. He argued about dishes. He did the West Coast paperwork. He was, by every indication, happy in a register he has never since reached. The collapse was not a collapse of love; it was a collision between her trauma-management strategy (silence, action, autonomy) and his rule-set (Cap's code, applied unmercifully to the person he loved most). He picked the code and he has known, ever since, that he picked wrong, and he cannot un-pick it.

**Trust / Safety.** Trust: structurally damaged; he believes her on operational matters and disbelieves her on matters of self. Safety: zero, in both directions — she is the person to whom he has done the worst harm of his life, and the person who has had the most opportunity to do harm to him. They are careful with each other in the way that people are careful with unexploded ordnance.

**Failure Mode.** Moral rigidity meeting concealment. If they were ever to try again — and the canon has flirted with it — the failure point would be the same: he applies the code because the code is the only fathering he ever had, and she withholds because withholding is how she survived.

**Leverage.** Anyone who threatens her gets the worst version of him. She herself can move him by a single sentence delivered without affect; she knows this and uses it sparingly.

---

#### Wanda Maximoff (Scarlet Witch)
*First contact:* Avengers #16 (1965), as fellow recruits to Cap's Kooky Quartet.

**History.** Nearly a decade as teammates with a low, persistent undercurrent (the early Englehart issues are explicit about his attraction; her commitment to Vision capped it). Reactivated after Vision's first dismantling and across her serial breakdowns. Subject was killed during her *Disassembled* psychotic break (Avengers #500), and resurrected by her in *House of M* — the most metaphysically intimate act anyone has ever performed on him. The post-*House of M* sequence in which he tracks her down and they spend a single night together (New Avengers #26, 2007) is the single most psychologically loaded sexual encounter in his published life: he sleeps with the woman who killed him and brought him back, partly to forgive her, partly to verify that he is alive.

**Dynamics.** Asymmetric and tender. She is, in his internal economy, simultaneously the agent of his death, the agent of his resurrection, a grieving widow, and an old crush. He treats her with a gentleness that is uncharacteristic and unmistakable. She, when sane, treats him as one of the few teammates who never feared her.

**Trust / Safety.** Trust: high in person, abstract in principle (he knows what she can do without meaning to). Safety: catastrophically low in any cosmic-stakes scenario, intimately high in a quiet room.

**Failure Mode.** Her reality-warping under stress. There is no defense; he has accepted this and folded the risk into the relationship.

**Leverage.** She does not weaponize it. He would not survive it if she did. The relationship persists in part because she has never once attempted to.

---

#### Jessica Drew (Spider-Woman)
*First sustained contact:* New Avengers era (2005 onward).

**History.** Bunkmate-adjacent on multiple long-form Avengers deployments. A brief, mostly-implied physical interval during the New Avengers period; a closer ongoing friendship that has outlasted it. She is one of perhaps four people who can call him at three in the morning and get a coherent answer.

**Dynamics.** Less freighted than the Romanoff or Morse channels — closer to the kind of relationship two professionals develop when they have repeatedly saved each other's lives and discovered they are also funny together. The sexual interval was, on his side, a brief experiment in *intimacy without history*, and on hers a similar gesture. Both seem to have concluded that the friendship was the more valuable yield.

**Trust / Safety.** Trust: high. Safety: relatively high, by his standards — she is one of the lovers who did not cost him a piece of his foundation.

**Failure Mode.** Drift. The relationship has no engine of its own; it runs on proximity.

**Leverage.** Modest. She can ask him for help and he will come; she rarely asks.

---

#### Kate Bishop (the deliberately non-sexual intimate)
Mapped fully in Section 5 / Relationships II. Listed here only to flag the structural fact: she is the woman to whom he has not done what he does, and the narrative protects this rigorously. Were the protection to fail, it would be the worst thing he ever did to a person. Both author and character appear to know this.

---

### II. RIVALS

#### Tony Stark (Iron Man)
*First contact:* the man on the poster he saw at the fair. The hero who made him want to be a hero. Also, by issue two of his costumed career, the man he was attempting to assault on the Black Widow's behalf.

**History.** Sixty years of teammate-rival oscillation. They have been founding-era Avengers together, West Coast Avengers (Tony funded the team Subject built), antagonists across *Civil War* (Subject anti-registration, Tony pro-), reconciled, re-antagonized, reconciled. The fundamental shape is constant: Tony is the institution, Subject is the rank-and-file, Tony is the man with the resources, Subject is the man with the bill.

**Dynamics.** Class-coded almost from the first panel. Subject's anti-authoritarianism finds its purest expression here because Tony is authority with money attached. He calls Tony "Stark" when he is angry and "Tony" when he is not, and the frequency of the former across his published life trends upward.

**Trust / Safety.** Trust: operational, conditional. He will follow Tony into combat; he will not follow Tony into a policy meeting. Safety: low — Tony's mistakes have killed friends of his, and Subject keeps a ledger.

**Failure Mode.** Tony makes a top-down call that violates the populist code, Subject objects with humor, Tony overrides, Subject quits, returns, repeats.

**Leverage.** Tony can leverage him by pointing out that the work needs doing; Subject can leverage Tony by refusing the work and walking. Tony hates this leverage and Subject knows it.

---

#### John Walker (U.S.Agent)
*First sustained contact:* West Coast Avengers era, after Cap's *Captain* interregnum.

**History.** Imposed on Subject's team by national-security fiat. The two are temperamental opposites — Walker is law-and-order, hierarchical, brittle-righteous; Subject is populist, insubordinate, ironic. They nearly came to blows on a near-weekly basis across the late WCA run.

**Dynamics.** Rivalry as friction without resolution. Walker triggers every authoritarian-allergy reflex Subject carries, and Subject triggers every legitimacy-anxiety reflex Walker carries. Neither has ever convinced the other of anything.

**Trust / Safety.** Trust: tactical only. Safety: surprisingly high — neither has ever sold the other out, despite ample opportunity. The professional floor holds where the personal ceiling cannot rise.

**Failure Mode.** Verbal escalation into physical. They have brawled. It resolved nothing and was understood by both as a kind of release.

**Leverage.** Mutual minimal. Walker cannot move Subject; Subject cannot move Walker; they coexist in the same field by sheer attritional habit.

---

#### Wonder Man (Simon Williams)
*First contact:* Avengers era; cohabitants of the West Coast roster.

**History.** Long-running low-grade rivalry over Bobbi Morse, with a layer of class friction (Simon was an actor; Subject was a carnie) and a layer of power-asymmetry resentment (Simon is ionic; Subject is meat). The rivalry has never quite ignited because Simon is too easygoing to take it up and Subject is too self-aware to insist on it.

**Dynamics.** Mostly performative. Subject needles, Simon shrugs, Subject needles harder, Simon shrugs harder.

**Trust / Safety.** Trust: high. Safety: high. The rivalry is theatrical and both men know it.

**Failure Mode.** The Bobbi triangle, if reactivated, could turn real. It has not, for a long time.

**Leverage.** None operationally significant.

---

#### Norman Osborn
*First sustained contact:* Dark Reign era, in which Osborn took over national security apparatus and installed a sociopath in Subject's old Ronin/Hawkeye costume.

**History.** Osborn putting Bullseye — the man who has tried to kill him repeatedly and who at one point murdered a partner he cared about — into his identity and parading him as a public-facing Avenger is the most targeted insult anyone has ever delivered to Subject's professional dignity. Subject's response (New Avengers #50; Dark Reign: The List — Avengers) was to attempt a public unilateral assassination of Osborn live on cable news. It failed; he was captured; the rest of the team retrieved him.

**Dynamics.** This is the rivalry in which Subject's hyperactive conscience went briefly silent. He did not want to arrest Osborn; he wanted to kill him on camera so the country could see. The aberration is diagnostic: identity-theft via Bullseye-in-his-costume struck at the *earn-the-right-to-be-here* substrate, and the entire stack collapsed into murderous purpose.

**Trust / Safety.** Trust: zero. Safety: zero. Osborn knows where his exposed nerve is and has, since, repeatedly pressed it.

**Failure Mode.** Subject's own. Osborn can elicit from him a version of himself Subject cannot otherwise reach.

**Leverage.** Osborn has it; Subject does not.

---

### III. ENEMIES

#### Bullseye (Lester)
*First contact:* Daredevil-adjacent crossovers, and the unforgettable Dark Reign sequence above.

**History.** The dark mirror — a man with comparable preternatural aim and the ethical loading of an industrial accident. Every face-off has been close, and several have ended with Subject getting up out of considerable damage on willpower alone. Bullseye is the only fighter in Subject's published record who has consistently been able to *hurt* him in the way Subject most fears: contemptuously, without effort, as a routine matter.

**Dynamics.** Bullseye treats Subject as a hobby. Subject treats Bullseye as evidence — proof of what the skill becomes if it grows in soil his happened not to grow in. The Dark Reign costume-theft converted this from professional rivalry into something nearer to personal vendetta.

**Trust / Safety.** N/A. Trust: zero. Safety: zero.

**Failure Mode.** Subject loses tactical patience when Bullseye is in the room, and tactical patience is what makes Subject elite. He overpresses. He has bled for this.

**Leverage.** Bullseye can pull Subject into bad ground by threatening innocents; Subject knows this and goes anyway.

---

#### Crossfire (William Cross)
*First contact:* Hawkeye vol. 1 #1 (1983).

**History.** The mercenary whose sonic torture-attack drove Subject to bite a sonic arrowhead and detonate it to break a gag — the act that took most of his hearing. Crossfire is, in a literal medical sense, the man who made him deaf.

**Dynamics.** Subject does not talk about this. He took the hearing damage as the cost of doing business and filed Crossfire away as a recurring nuisance rather than a defining adversary.
